Event handling and order 

There are two basic ways to arrange the order in which events that have multiple handlers and actions 
execute those handlers and actions. 

Event handler initial sequence 

When an event handler is first defined and saved, the system automatically assigns it a handler sequence 
number. When the event handler is first saved, the system checks to see if there are already any other 
handlers associated with the named event. Depending on the results of that check, the system then 
assigns 1 to the handler (if there are no other handlers associated with the event) or the next available 
integer (if there are other handlers associated with the event). 

In general, then, if an event uses multiple event handlers, by default, the system uses the handler 
sequence numbers to determine the order in which the handlers execute. 

It is possible, however, to indirectly alter this default order. This is done either by: 

•  Using the Keep With and Chronology fields on the Event Handlers form. 
•  Or 
•  Moving your own adjacent event handlers up or down in the sequence, using the Event Handler 

Sequence form. 

The following is a high-level overview of a typical process for altering the default order in which event 
handlers execute using the Keep With and Chronology fields on the Event Handlers form: 

Step 

How to alter the order of a handler using the Keep With and Chronology fields 

1 

2 

Select an event handler  

In the grid view, select an event handler that has your Access As value. 

Determine the event handler you want to use as a reference point and anchor for the 
selected handler. Select that reference event handler from the Keep With drop-down list.  

Note: This step is not required if you are using the First or Last option in the Chronology 
field. 

3 

Select the option you want the current handler to use from the Chronology drop-down list.  

This sets what the current handler will use with respect to the handler you selected in Step 
2. Options include: 

•  First – Executes the current handler before any other handlers. 
•  Before – Executes the current handler just before the referenced handler. 
•  Instead – Executes the current handler in place of the referenced handler. In this case, 

the referenced (original) handler does not execute at all.  

•  Exclusively Instead – Executes the current handler instead of the referenced handler 
and any other handler that may be referenced to execute instead of that same handler. 

•  After – Executes the current handler just after the referenced handler. 
•  Last – Executes the current handler after all other handlers. 

88   Lesson 4: Designing events and handlers 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
For more information about reordering event handlers, including some detailed examples, 
see Appendix D, Synchronization of Metadata. 

Resequencing event handlers 

Use the Event Handler Sequence form to change the sequence in which your adjacent event handlers 
execute for a specified event. 

The Event Handler Sequence form is intended to be accessed as a linked form, from 
the Event Handlers form only, using the Resequence button. If you open it in 
standalone mode, the results can be unpredictable. 

The Access As identifier must be considered when resequencing handlers. Here are some tips that 
restrict when you can use the Event Sequence form:  

•  Handlers that have the same Access As value: 

•  Yes, you can use the Event Handler Sequence form to change the order of event handlers.  
•  The handlers must be grouped together (that is, adjacent to one another in the sequence), 

and within the group.  

•  Handlers that have a different Access As value: 

•  No, you cannot use this form to change the sequence of event handlers.  
•  To change the order of your event handlers with respect to those of others (that is, with 
different Access As values), use the Keep With and Chronology fields on the Event 
Handlers form. 

The following is a high-level overview of a typical process for changing the sequence in which event 
handlers execute using the Event Handlers Sequence form: 

Step 

How to change the sequence of a handler using the Event Handlers Sequence form 

1 

2 

3 

Open an event handler  

In the grid view, select an event handler that has your Access As value. 

Click the Resequence button on the Event Handlers form 

Move the handler up or down in the sequence 

Click the Up or Down button to move the selected handler up or down in the sequence, 
keeping in mind the restrictions mentioned above. 

Note: If you try to violate those restrictions, the system generates an error and you cannot 
complete the move. 

4 

Save the new sequence

Ordering event actions 

A single event handler can contain multiple event actions. When you define an event action, you must 
assign an action sequence number to it (in the Action Sequence field of the Event Actions form). You 
can assign any number you want in that field, and the system automatically sorts the actions in the 
correct sequence on the Event Handlers form. When the event handler executes, the system uses this 
Action Sequence number to determine the order in which the actions execute. 

The only exception to this rule is that, if you select an action (other than 1) in the Initial Action field of the 
Event Handlers form, then processing of the event actions begins with the designated action and 
proceeds from there.  

Example  Using the Initial Action field 

Let’s say you have four event actions associated with a handler, and have numbered them 1, 2, 3, and 4.  

You later decide you want action number 3 to be the starting point. You select 3 in the Initial Action field 
of the Event Handlers form. In this case, only actions 3 and 4 would execute. The system would skip 
over actions 1 and 2.  

Note: You could later execute these actions by using an action type of Branch or Goto, with one of these 
actions as the destination. 

End of example

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
Determining names of IDO collections and 
components 

To create custom event handlers and actions, you are often required to know the internal names of the 
collections (known internally as "IDO collections") and the components you want to refer to.  

For example, to set up a handler, you often need the name of the IDO collection associated with a 
particular form. To include dynamic content in the subject or body of a message, you often must know the 
internal name of a property within that IDO. 

But what if you do not know those names? How can you find what you need? 

Determining the name of an IDO  

The following is a high-level overview of a typical process for determining the name of an IDO for an 
event handler definition: 

Step 

How to determine the name of an IDO 

1 

Open the form that uses the IDO collection you need 

For example, if you are setting up an event handler to work with customer records, you 
would open the Customers form. 

2 

3 

4 

Enter design mode for that form  

Locate the Form properties sheet  

If it is not showing, from the View menu, select the Form Properties option. 

Select the Collections tab 

The names of all IDO collections associated with that form are displayed in the Collections 
list at the top of the form. Usually, there is only one collection, which makes it easy to figure 
out.  

For example, the Customers form uses the SL.SLCustomers IDO. The name of the IDO 
collection is SLCustomers. 

If more than one collection is listed, you might have to take further steps to determine which 
collection is the one you need. 

The internal name of the IDO is that part of the IDO name that displays after the period.

Discarding the metadata cache 

Metadata is a set of data that describes and gives information about other data.  

As you use the Application Event System, certain summary event metadata is cached in memory for 
faster performance. You should discard the metadata cache periodically. This should be done, at a 
minimum, after doing development work, before testing, and after synchronizing the metadata on your 
system. Ideally, you should discard the IDO metadata cache after making changes to events, handlers, 
actions, triggers, or global constants.  

Here are some considerations for discarding the cache: 

•  Any event metadata that is not referenced within two minutes is automatically discarded from the 
cache. That is why you might notice that things work the way you expect, even without manually 
discarding the cached metadata. We still recommend that, as a precaution, you manually discard 
the cached metadata to be sure. 
If you have multiple utility servers in your system, you must discard cached metadata for each 
utility server on which metadata might have been cached. The best way to do this is to unload the 
global objects.  

• 

There are four ways you can discard the cached metadata: 

•  Unload global objects by pressing Crl+U 
•  Restart the IDO Runtime Service on the utility server  
•  Manually from the IDO Runtime Development Server  
•  Use the Discard Cache button on the Utilities tab of the Configuration Manager 

We’ll look at the first three methods in more detail.  

Unload global objects 

With the correct system settings, you can have the system discard the cached metadata automatically 
every time you unload all global objects.  

Here is how to change the settings and the shortcut for unloading global objects: 

If you want to… 

Then do this… 

Change settings to be able to discard the cached 
metadata when you unload global objects 

Select User Preferences from the View 
menu in WinStudio. 

Click the Runtime Behaviors tab. 

Select the Unload IDO Metadata With 
Forms check box. 

Click OK. 

Unload global objects (and discard cached metadata) 

Click Ctrl+U. 

While working on event metadata, periodically unload global objects, and the cached metadata is 
automatically discarded with the global objects. 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18) 

93 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Restart the IDO Runtime Service 

You can discard the cached metadata by manually stopping and restarting the IDO Runtime Service on 
the utility server. This works because the metadata cache is not saved when the service is stopped. 

Here is how to discard cached metadata by restarting the IDO Runtime Service: 

If you want to… 

Then do this… 

Stop the IDO Runtime 
Service 

Open Control Panel on the utility server. 

Select Administrative Tools > Services. 

Double-click Infor Framework IDO Runtime Services. 

Click Stop in the Infor Framework IDO Runtime Services Properties 
dialog box. 

Restart the IDO Runtime 
Service 

Verify that the IDO Runtime Services Properties dialog box indicates 
that the service has stopped.  

Click Start. 

Manually from the IDO Runtime Development Server 

If you are using a local installation of the IDO Runtime Development Server, you can discard the cached 
metadata manually. 

Here is how to manually discard cached metadata in the IDO Runtime Development Server: 

If you want to… 

Then do this… 

Discard cached metadata in the IDO 
Runtime Development Server 

Open the IDO Runtime Development Server. 

Select the configuration for which you want to discard 
the cached IDO and event metadata. 

Select Discard IDO Metadata Cache from the 
Configuration menu. 

If you are creating and using your own custom events and handlers, we recommend that 
you discard the metadata cache periodically. This should be done after doing development 
work, before testing, and after synchronizing your metadata on your system.

New Workflow Wizard form 

The New WorkFlow Wizard is new to CloudSuite 9. You can use this wizard in place of the Event 
Handlers form when setting up simple notification events. The wizard cannot support events for complex 
notifications or for those that use that use prompt-type actions such as approval notices.   

Creating workflows with the wizard 

Users such as purchasing managers or executives can use the New Workflow Wizard to quickly create 
workflows (event handlers and actions) for some basic notification scenarios. For example, a purchasing 
manager can build a workflow to "Notify me when a PO line is created for more than $1000." 

As you make simple choices in the wizard, behind the scenes the system is creating event handler and 
event actions metadata that can later be viewed or edited in the standard Application Event System 
forms. 

Here is how to build a simple notification workflow: 

On the first page of the New Workflow Wizard, specify one of these options: 

Option 

Explanatory details 

Notify Me When 

Select this radio button if you want to assign the people who should receive a 
notification when the specified change is made to the system.  

For example, if the sales manager and the credit manager should receive 
notification when anyone adds a new customer, use this option.  

Notify You When 

Select this radio button if the originator (the person who makes or causes the 
specified change) should receive a notification in their CloudSuite Inbox. 

For example, if a salesperson should receive notification when they add a new 
customer to the system, use this option.  

Build from 
Scratch 

Customize 
Resulting 
Workflow 

Select this option and click Finish to exit the workbench and use the standard 
forms to build the workflow. 

Select the Customize Resulting Workflow check box if you want to open the 
event handler you created in the standard forms when you finish building the 
workflow through the wizard.  

Note: This option is enabled only if you selected one of the Notify options.  

Next 

Click Next to accept your selections and move to the next page of the wizard.

Notification of changes to an existing record 

We have seen how to build events and handlers for simple notifications. Now we will practice making a 
minor change to a notification.  

This exercise is similar to exercise 3.4, except that, instead of notifying the credit manager when a 
customer is added to the database, we want to create an event and handler that notifies the credit 
manager whenever a customer’s credit limit is changed.  

As with the first scenario, we can use an existing framework event. This time we will use 
IdoOnItemUpdate and create our own handler for it. And again, because we are simply sending out a 
notification and the system is not waiting for a response from the credit manager, we can make it an 
asynchronous event handler.

Notification that includes an old and new value 

Notifications can range from the very simple, to increasingly complex. In the next exercise, we will 
practice making a moderately complex change to a notification.  

In this scenario, we want to notify the inventory stock clerk automatically whenever an item’s lot size 
changes. In the message that is sent, we want to include both the previous lot size and the new lot size. 
We also want to let the stock clerk know who initiated the change. 

Once again, we will use an existing framework event, IdoOnItemUpdate, and create our own handler for 
it. Because this handler needs to retrieve the "before" property value, we must make it synchronous, so 
that during handler execution we can retrieve from the database the original row that is being updated, 
before it is updated by the IDO request. 

This event handler requires three actions: 

•  One to check whether the Lot Size field has been changed and, if not, finish. 
•  One to retrieve the row being updated and both the original and new values for the Lot Size field. 
•  One to send the notification to the inventory stock clerk.

checks for changes in lot size, the second retrieves both the old and new lot sizes, and the 
third sends a notification message.

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  109 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
About message-related forms 

Event message-related forms are used to view, sort, file, respond to, and send messages generated 
within the Application Event System.  

The Application Event System uses these message-related forms: 

Inbox form 

• 
•  Saved Messages form 
•  Send Message form 

The Infor Application Event System can be configured to use external email systems such 
as Microsoft® Outlook® in addition to the system message forms.  

110   Lesson 5: Viewing event messages 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Inbox form 

The Inbox form can be used with the Application Event System or it can also be used to communicate 
with other users in your CloudSuite environment. The Inbox form displays system messages that can 
come from three possible sources: 

•  Application events that use a Notify action type 
•  Application events that use a Prompt action type 
•  Communications initiated and sent by individual users to other users on the system 

The Inbox is not a full working email system. For example, you may notice that there is no way to 
compose a new message from the Inbox. (To send messages, you must go the Send Message form.) 
The Inbox is primarily a way to read and respond to messages.  

If you have a new message in the Inbox, an envelope icon will appear in your system tray. You can click 
the icon to open the Inbox form. You can mark messages as read and respond to certain types of 
messages. 

The Inbox form can be accessed in several different ways: 

•  From the View menu, by selecting the Inbox Form option 
• 
• 

In the Windows® taskbar (notifications area), by double clicking the Inbox notification icon 
In the same ways that any other forms are accessed 

This form displays only those messages which are still in the recipient’s Inbox folder and not messages 
that have been moved to other folders. To view those messages, recipients must use the Saved 
Messages form. The Inbox form also does not allow recipients to move messages to other folders. To do 
that, recipients must use the Saved Messages form.  

When a message is received, if the recipient has set options to be notified, the system alerts the recipient 
with the selected notifications. Note: For more information, see "Notifications Settings" in the online help. 

Recipients can mark messages as read and, depending on how and why the message was sent, make 
other responses.  

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  111 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Variables in event messages 

Some messages in the Inbox involve variables. For each variable, recipients might be able to: 

•  Provide an optional response 
•  Provide a mandatory response 
•  Only read the variable value 
•  Not see the variable value at all 

Setting variable access 

The effective visibility and writability of each variable displayed on the Inbox form is determined by two 
things: 

•  What type of action generated the message (Notify or Prompt) 
•  The (optional) variable access level as specified: 

o  On the Event Actions form for the action itself and/or  
o  On the Event Variable Groups form for the event handler’s initial state and/or  
o  On the Event Action Notify or Event Action Prompt form for the action about the payload 
status of the property that corresponds to the variable, when the handler is associated with 
an IDO event. 

For Notify type messages, the default for variable access is Read-Only. You can use the variable access 
options to override this to Hidden for each variable. 

For Prompt type messages, the default for variable access is Writable. You can use the variable access 
options to override this to Hidden, Read-Only, or Mandatory for each variable. 

To change the value of a variable that might appear with a message in the Inbox form, you can do any of 
these actions: 

•  Specify the data using the Variables tab on the Inbox form as part of a response to a Prompt 

action 

•  Use a Set Values event action with the function syntax: SETVARVALUES(PropertyName=name) 
•  Use any of various event actions that can set a variable on output using the function syntax: 

RV(PropertyName) 

Setting translatable captions for variables 

In the Inbox form’s Variable tab, the Caption column displays the contents of the notify or prompt 
message's variable captions in the current user’s language. This assumes that: 

•  The caption component attributes are set to interpret the bound contents. 
•  The caption contains a translatable string name. 

For payload variables resulting from an IDO event, this string name might come from an IDO property’s 
label string ID. For non-payload variables that are created by an event action, you define this string name 
using the Event Actions form, Variable Access tab. 

112   Lesson 5: Viewing event messages 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
Prompts and responses 

If the message in the Inbox form is the result of a system-generated prompt, each recipient can respond 
to the prompt. In such cases, the system must be set up to do the following: 

•  Wait for responses  
•  Handle responses as they are received  
•  Act when responses are not received within a specified timeout period 

Message prompts typically display a set of choices for the recipient, usually by means of a set of voting 
buttons. These buttons display in the Response tab area of the Inbox form. For example, a prompt might 
include buttons labeled: 

•  Approve / Disapprove (default option) 
•  Yes / No 
•  OK / Send More Info / Cancel 

Prompts and external email 

Prompts that are sent to external email addresses do not contain voting buttons. Instead they contain 
links that the recipient can use to respond.  

If the message was sent both to the recipient’s Inbox form and to external email, and the recipient 
responded to the email message, the message in the refreshed Inbox is marked as expired and the 
buttons are inactive, so the recipient cannot respond twice. 

Lesson 11 provides further details on using external email with the Application Event 
System.  

Setting up a prompt with choices 

To customize the choices for a prompt, you must include a Prompt action with a Choices parameter as 
part of the event action definition. This Choices parameter consists of the CHOICES function followed by 
a string expression that evaluates to a comma-separated list that contains an even number of elements 
(value/label pairs). For example, if you want the voting buttons to be labeled Yes and No, with 
corresponding values returned to the action to be 1 and 0, you could include this parameter: 
CHOICES("1,sYes,0,sNo") 

In this example, the strings "sYes" and "sNo" are WinStudio form strings. These have already been 
defined for the system as Yes and No, respectively. 

If you want your button labels to be localized, for the recipient, you must: 

•  Use names of existing form strings (as found in the Strings table). 

Or 

•  Add your own form strings, using the Strings form, and provide the necessary translations. Note: 
To open the Strings form, you must be in Design Mode and, from the Edit menu, select Strings. 

If localization is not an issue, you can also use a literal value that displays on the button verbatim. To 
specify the string as a literal value here, simply specify it as a list value. If the system does not find the 
string in the Strings table, the system automatically treats it as a literal value.

Tracking status forms 

Some application events can take a considerable amount of time to process, especially if they involve 
event messages that require responses from the recipients. The system provides several tools and forms 
that allow you to track the status of application events as they execute and after they have finished 
executing. Some of these forms also allow you to temporarily adjust the behavior of handler execution. 

These forms are located in the Explorer under Master Explorer > Modules > System > Event System.  

These forms can all be used to track various aspects of event system status: 

•  Event Status form 
•  Event Handler Status form 
•  Event Queue form 
•  Event Revisions form 
•  Event Handler Revisions form 
•  Suspended Updates form 

Initially, these forms can be accessed only by members of the System Administration authorization group. 

118   Lesson 6: Tracking event system status 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Event Status form 

Use the Event Status form to view: 

•  The status of events that are currently running. 
•  The history of events that have finished running. 

The Event Status form has five tabs: 

Tab name 

Tab description 

Event tab 

This tab provides options to filter for events and handlers in various states and 
make it easier to locate specific ones. 

For example, suppose you want to find data about all events that are currently 
suspended. With Filter in Place, you would select the Suspended check box and 
then execute Filter-in-Place. 

Handlers tab 

This tab shows data about handlers that are currently processing or have finished 
processing.  

Voting tab 

This tab shows data about the voting status of a Prompt action type. 

Parameters tab 

This tab shows data about the parameters associated with an event that is 
currently running. These include input parameters passed into the event, as well 
as output parameters created by handlers’ actions. 

Output 
Parameters tab 

This tab shows data about the output parameters of an event that has finished 
running. 

The Event Status form can be helpful when you are not seeing the behavior you expected from an event. 
Here are things to search for in the Event tab:  

•  Records with a status of “failure” and have a finish time 
•  Records for which you are the originator 
•  Records that have a status of “running” and do not have a finish time

Event Queue form 

The Event Queue form displays a list of all asynchronous events and event handlers that the system has 
queued for processing.  

Events on the queue are processed in FIFO (first in, first out) order. The ID number on this form indicates 
the order in which events are queued for processing. 

This form also displays other information about events and event handlers that have been queued for 
processing. Each event or event handler that has been queued is displayed as a separate record in the 
grid view. 

All information on the Event Queue form is display only.

Event and event handler revisions 

We learned that whenever an event or handler revision is revised, the system copies all the event's 
handlers and actions to a read-only table. The event or handler then uses the data in this read-only table 
when executing the handlers and actions, until a new revision is created. 

There are two forms that contain display-only information about revisions:   

•  Event Revisions form 
•  Event Handler Revisions form 

Event Revisions form 

The Event Revisions form displays information about the event revisions associated with events. 

Event Handler Revisions form 

The Event Handler Revisions form shows information about event handler revisions associated with 
event handlers. All information on this form is display-only. The reason for this is that some running or 
finished handlers are using the metadata in this revision to complete their processing. To change the data 
for this event handler, you must use the Event Handlers form. 

The Event Handler Revisions form can be opened by clicking the Event Handlers 
Revision button found on the Event Revisions form.   

Event and event handler revisions 

The system creates a set of event handler revisions the first time: 

•  The event is generated or any of its handlers executes. 
•  The event is generated after any of its constituent handlers or their actions have been modified in 

any way. 

•  Any of the event’s handlers executes after any of its constituent actions have been modified in 

any way. 

Modifications can include additions, changes, or deletions to the handlers or actions associated with the 
event or handler. 

It is important to understand that these forms are display-only forms. You will not perform any action on 
these forms. They are reference forms that show you all revisions that exist in the system for a particular 
event or event handler.   

When the revision is created, the system copies all the event's handlers and actions to a read-only table. 
This means that the events and event handlers are saved off and persist in the system. The event or 
handler then uses the data in this read-only table when executing the handlers and actions, until a new 
revision is created. 

Revisions are used to help ensure that the metadata used by an event and its handlers and actions is not 
altered while the event is executing. In some cases, it can take the system some time to finish executing 
an event's handlers, either because of the processing time involved, or because the system is waiting for 
some input or response before it can continue. It is possible that someone could make changes to the 

122   Lesson 6: Tracking event system status 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
event's handlers and actions while the event is processing or waiting, and that these changes could affect 
the execution of the event that is in progress. 

Revisions were developed to address this kind of potential problem. When an event fires, the event and 
its handlers use the revisions that are in effect at the time they start executing until they are finished. 

Example  Changing the person who will give manager approval 

Suppose you are using an event to send notices to a manager when a customer order is more than 
$10,000. The manager must approve the order before it can be processed. 

During a transfer of responsibilities from one manager to another, a new manager is assigned the 
responsibility of approving such orders. The system administrator makes the change of notice to the 
appropriate event action. 

However, the original manager still has a few orders pending approval. These orders continue to use the 
metadata for the revision in effect at the time they were created, awaiting that manager's approval. In the 
meantime, the new manager receives notices for any subsequent orders, because the first new order 
generates a new revision using the information for the new manager. 

End of example

Suspended Updates form 

The Suspended Updates form is another status form. It displays a list of all the update actions that are 
currently in a suspended state. This form also allows you to take selected updates out of suspension 
manually. 

Review of suspended records 

On the Event Handlers form you can suspend a handler and it will wait for an adjourning action, which is 
an action that causes it to proceed. Typically, this is used for event handlers that require approval. If they 
choose to not approve a record, then we do not want the disapproved record committed in the system. 
Any record that has not been approved (i.e., that is either disapproved or has had no response) will be 
suspended. The Suspended Updates form displays all these records.   

Example  New purchase order record in suspense 

Suppose you have created an event handler for new purchase orders that is a prompt type (you are 
requesting approval from a manager). You selected the Suspend check box on the Event Handlers 
form.   

You then create a new purchase order, and the event handler fires off a request to the manager asking 
for manager approval. If the manager sends approval, the system will commit the record. But you wait for 
24 hours and cannot find any record of the purchase order. You think that the manager either 
disapproved or did not respond at all, and the record is being held in a suspended state.   

You open the Suspended Updates form and can locate the record. This is the only place in the system 
where you can view the record; however, you can also see the event actions that would be running, 
waiting for a response.  

End of example

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
About requesting approvals 

Setting up an event handler to request approval requires using an action type we have not yet used called 
“prompt.” A prompt action asks (or prompts) and sends a message, but also asks the recipient to send a 
response to the message. This differs from notification actions that require no response.  

In our next scenario, we want to send a message to the purchasing manager whenever a purchase order 
(PO) is added. This message prompts the purchasing manager for approval of the PO. The purchasing 
manager can indicate approval (or disapproval) by clicking a button in the message itself. If approved, the 
system adds the PO; if not, the system does not add the PO. 

As with the previous exercises, the system framework has a built-in event, IdoOnItemInsert, which we can 
use with our handler. The handler itself requires two event actions: a “prompt” action to send the approval 
request to the manager, and a “fail” action to tell the system what to do if approval is denied.   

You must tell the system how to evaluate the response received by the manager. This is done by adding 
an event action parameter condition for the function called VOTINGRESULT to the “fail” event action, and 
assigning values to “approved” or “denied” responses. 

Exercise 7.1: Approving a purchase order 

In this exercise, you will set up an event handler to request manager approval for all new 
purchase orders. This event handler will contain two event actions. 

Exercise steps 

Part 1: Create the global constant for Purchasing Manager

2.  Click Filter in Place.  

3.  Click Create a new object in the current collection. 

4.  Type PurchasingMgr in the Name field.  

5.  Type <your user ID> in the Value field.  

6.  Click Save.  

7.  Close the Event Global Constants form.  

Part 2: Create the event handler 

1.  Open the Event Handlers form. 

2.  Click Filter in Place. 

3.  Click Create a new object in the current collection. 

4.  Select IdoOnItemInsert from the Event Name drop-down list.  

5.  Type Approval of a New Purchase Order in the Handler Description field.  

6.  Select SLPos in the Applies to Objects drop-down list.  

Note: You can type SLPo* in the Applies to Objects field to narrow the choices in the drop-down 
list.

Event handler diagrams 

You may find it easier to build or work with an event handler if you can visualize the workflow. You can 
access a flow chart diagram for any event handler by clicking the Diagram button on the Event Handlers 
form.  

You can use the Event Handler Diagram form to: 

•  View a graphical (diagrammatic) representation of an event handler and its actions.  
•  Access the Event Actions form to modify event actions.  
•  Add event actions to the flow.  
•  Delete event actions from the flow.  
•  Edit the final diagram before copying, printing, or saving.  
•  Copy the diagram to the system clipboard.  
•  Print the diagram.  
•  Save the diagram as a graphics file.  

For example, the diagram for exercise 7.1 looks similar to the diagram shown below: 

Event handler with two event actions – prompt and fail 

Accessing the Event Actions form to modify event actions 

To access the Event Actions form for a selected event action in the flow: 

In the diagram display, double-click the node for the event action you want to edit.  

• 
•  When the Event Actions form opens, edit the action as desired.  
•  Save your changes and close the form.  
•  When the system asks whether you want to update the event handler diagram with the latest 

changes, respond Yes.  

Adding event actions 

To add an event action to an event handler flow: 

•  Click the Event Actions menu bar on the left edge of the diagram display area.  

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  131 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
•  Drag and drop the new event action into the diagram display area.  
•  When the Event Actions form opens, use it to define the new action.  
•  When finished, save the new action and close the form.  

Deleting actions 

To delete an event action from an event handler flow: 

In the diagram display, select the node for the event action you want to delete.  

• 
•  Right-click the node.  
•  From the context menu, select Delete Event Action.  

Editing the diagram display 

To edit the diagram display: 

•  Select the node that you want to move.  
•  Click and drag the node to the desired location.  

Note: Any changes you make to the diagram are not persistent; that is, they only last if you make no 
more changes to the event handler flow. Therefore, if you want to make manual adjustments to the layout 
of the diagram before printing it, for example, these manual adjustments should be the very last thing you 
do. 

Copying the diagram to the system clipboard 

To copy a diagram to the system clipboard: 

•  Right-click anywhere inside the diagram display area.  
•  From the context menu, select Copy to Clipboard.  
•  Once the diagram is copied to the system clipboard, you can paste it into another program, such 

as MS Word®, PowerPoint®, or a graphics program. 

Printing a diagram 

To print a diagram: 

•  Right-click anywhere inside the diagram display area.  
•  From the context menu, select Print.  
•  The system prints the diagram on whatever printer is designated as the user's default printer. 

Saving a diagram 

To save a diagram as a graphics file: 

•  Right-click anywhere inside the diagram display area.  
•  From the context menu, select Save To Image.  
• 

In the Save As dialog box, provide a name for the image file and then click Save.

Lesson 8: Adding information 

Estimated time 

.5 hours 

Learning objectives 

After completing this lesson, you will be able to: 

•  Explain how to set up an event to add information to a record. 

Topics 

•  About adding information to a record 

134   Lesson 8: Adding information 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
About adding information to a record 

You can use the Application Event System to send a message (a prompt) asking a recipient to provide 
new information, such as a value. This new information can then be automatically added to an existing 
record.  

When adding new information, the recipient can be given the ability to enter information by selecting from 
a set of choices (e.g., voting buttons) or as a free-form response, (e.g., by typing certain values). Note: 
Free-form functionality is only available when sending the prompt via the CloudSuite messaging service 
to a recipient’s Inbox form.  

If you want to… 

Then… 

Respond to a message requesting new 
information 

•  Open the Inbox form. 
•  Open the message with the request. 

•  Type a value on the Variables tab of the message. 
•  Save the modified Inbox record. 

•  Click the Post button on the Response tab to 

register the response.  

You can define an event handler to send prompts for new information to external email addresses, but 
must provide a set of choices from which the recipient can choose, i.e., by voting for a selection. The 
system cannot accept free-form values from external email prompts.

140   Lesson 9: Requesting approvals - advanced 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
About multiple and complex approvals 

In addition to basic approvals, the Application Event System can also support multiple and complex 
approvals. These approvals involve multiple people and/or multiple criteria. Here are two examples: 

•  Additional individuals are prompted to approve only if certain predefined criteria are met 
•  Multiple people are prompted to give approval, but the ultimate approval decision is based on a 

tally of their “votes” 

The event handler diagram below shows a complex approval process requiring fourteen event actions.  

Event handler diagram for three levels of approval 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  141 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Note that one set of four actions (2-4) is repeated three times: Set variables, Send prompt, Wait for voting 
results, Evaluate whether the results are approved.  

142   Lesson 9: Requesting approvals - advanced 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
Approval by multiple levels of management 

This exercise will demonstrate approval prompts being sent out to multiple people based on predefined 
criteria, in this case a purchase order status change to “Ordered” and the amount of the purchase order.  

We will set up an event handler and event actions so that when a purchase order (PO) status is changed 
to Ordered, it requires the approval of the purchasing manager. At the same time, if the PO is for more 
than $100,000, the PO also requires the approval of the purchasing manager’s supervisor. Finally, if the 
PO is for more than $1,000,000, the PO requires the further approval of a senior executive. 

If the PO is disapproved at any level, the PO is rolled back to the previous values, and any changes made 
to it are lost. While the PO is in the process of being approved, it remains suspended until approval or 
disapproval is determined. This means, among other things, that if one or more approvers fail to respond 
to the request, the PO is locked and cannot be changed until all required approvers respond. 

For this exercise, we will: 

•  Use the same event global constant for the purchasing manager (PurchasingMgr) that we used 

for a previous exercise. 

•  Create new event globals constants for the purchasing supervisor and purchasing senior 
executive, PO values for each management level, and the approval message content.  

•  Use the IdoOnItemUpdate framework event for the SLPos IDO. This will cause the event to be 
generated whenever a PO record is updated either in the Purchase Orders form or by another 
process that attempts to update that record. 

•  Use an action type called a branch to evaluate each response received (approved or not) and 

choose the next action based on that response.  

•  Pass property values and an identifying property (ItemId) to the event as input parameters so the 

system can store them with the event as event parameters. 

The variable named CountMethod is set to count the votes using the MinimumPercentage rule, which 
says that the first choice to reach a minimum percentage determines the next action. In this case, the 
minimum percentage is 100%, so all recipients must approve for the PO to reach final approval. If any 
recipient rejects the request, the entire request is rejected, no matter who has approved it to that point. 

The MinimumPercentage voting rule requires that you specify a minimum percentage for passage. This 
means that, in addition to the VOTINGRULE( ) keyword, you must also specify the MINIMUM( ) keyword 
as part of the variable definition. The resulting declaration for the Value column of the CountMethod 
variable is: VOTINGRULE(MinimumPercentage) MINIMUM(100).

Part 5: Create the event action #30-PROMPT 

1.  Click Create a new object in the current collection.  

2.  Type 30 in the Action Sequence field.

4.  Type TGC(POApprovalPrompt) in the Parameters tab text box.  

Because TGC( ) is a pre-parser function, you cannot use the Event Action 
Parameter forms to create or set it. You must specify this statement directly in the 
Parameters field of the Event Actions form. This also means that you cannot use 
the Check Syntax button to check the syntax. 

This statement performs a text evaluation of the POApprovalPrompt global constant 
to obtain the parameters for a prompt action. Part of this text evaluation includes an 
evaluation and insertion of the values for the two variables we set in the previous 
step. 

After evaluating the POApprovalPrompt global constant, this action also sends out 
the prompt message to the purchasing manager and suspends the handler pending 
the manager’s response. Because we did not specify any Variable Access rules, the 
message allows the purchasing manager to modify any variable values before 
approving it.

Framework events vs. developer-defined events 

One of the big similarities between the Form Event System and the Application Event System is, 
obviously, that they both deal with events. In both cases, the event itself is simply a uniquely named 
occurrence. Yes, that sounds a bit vague, but the central idea is that when that something happens, we 
can set up the system to do something else in response to that event.   

The chief difference between a form-level event and an application event is the way they are defined. 
Form events are typically defined by naming them and then assigning at least one event handler to deal 
with them, nearly always in response to some user action.  

The Application Event System takes a somewhat broader view of events. Events in the Application Event 
System can be one of two general types:  

•  Framework events 
•  Developer-defined events  
• 

We have been using framework events in all the exercises so far, so now let’s step back and review them 
once again. 

Framework events 

Framework events are events that Infor has predefined and built in to the system. These events—which 
include system actions like adding a record, modifying a record, deleting a record, and so on—cannot be 
generated programmatically. That is, you cannot define framework events; they simply get generated 
every time the system does something.  

Now, what this means is that events are constantly being generated in CloudSuite applications. Most of 
the time, you are not aware of them and the system does nothing in response to them. That is because, if 
no event handler has been defined to respond to an event, no response is generated. The event occurs, 
and that is that.  

We can, however, define event handlers to respond to these framework events, and that is a large part of 
what the Application Event System is about.  

Developer-defined events 

Developer-defined events, such as the custom events you create, are events that you can define yourself, 
by defining a new row on the Events form to respond to specific user actions or other system triggers.   

Developer-defined events can respond to: 

•  Event triggers 
•  User actions   

Developer-defined events that are based on user actions are similar to form events. These events require 
the user to take some action to which the event system then responds.  

The big difference here is a form event is limited to actions on a single form while the 
application event can involve multiple forms.   

156   Lesson 10: Generating events from within a form 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Developer-defined events that are based on event triggers are a little different. Typically, event triggers 
are things that happen within the system that might or might not involve user action of any kind. Here are 
a few examples: 

•  You can create an event handler that is designed to respond to an event at a certain time, or after 

a certain amount of time has passed.  

•  You can design an event handler to trigger when a certain currency amount has been exceeded.   
•  You can have an event that is generated based on some action involving a Web service or 

another application.  

The possibilities for triggering an event are nearly endless. 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  157 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Using the Application Event System within a form 

The next exercise is different from others because we will use a developer-designed event, not a 
framework event. All the exercises we have done previously were built on an existing framework event, 
for example IdoOnItemInsert. So far, we have not had to create an event, only event handlers and event 
actions.    

Not every scenario for which you want an event to occur will fall within the realm of existing framework 
events. To fulfill an organizational need, you may need to get creative to design a new event to be able to 
achieve your objectives.  

Here is the scenario for the next exercise: CloudSuite users have requested that the system administrator 
provide them with a means to submit information to the IT department from within the system. In this 
case, there is no existing framework event (such as an IT Issue IDO) and so we must build out the 
functionality based on actions that occur in the system by the user. You will set up the event and event 
handlers as you have in previous exercises, and then you will call to this event from within the new form 
you create using the action type called “Generate application event.”

Sending messages to external email 

When you define event actions that send messages to recipients, the Application Event System will send 
prompt and notification messages to the CloudSuite Inbox forms of those recipients. However, it is 
possible to send messages to recipients’ external email addresses as well.  

There are three action types that can generate messages sent to external email addresses: 

•  Notify 
•  Prompt 
•  Send Email 

If a user is set up to allow the system to "Send External Notifications," then a notify action sends the 
message both to the CloudSuite Inbox form and to the recipient’s inbox in an external email client such as 
Microsoft® Outlook®.  

Similarly, if a user is set up to allow the system to "Send external prompts," then a prompt action sends 
the message both to the CloudSuite Inbox form and to the recipient’s inbox in an external email client. 
There are some limitations on the format of prompt messages sent to external email addresses.  

If a user is configured to receive external email, then a “Send email” action sends the message to the 
recipient’s external email client, but does not send it to the CloudSuite Inbox form.  

The chart below summarizes where recipients will receive messages sent by the Application Event 
System:  

Action 
type 

Notify 

Prompt  

Message sent to Inbox 
form? 

Email sent? 

(for users set up to receive email) 

Yes 

Yes 

Yes 

Yes, but formatting restrictions will limit certain 
functionality 

Send Email 

No 

Yes 

164   Lesson 11: Setting up external email 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Format of external email 

A message that is sent to a recipient’s external email system is an HTML-formatted email that consists of 
these parts: 

•  Original subject in Subject line 
•  Category 
•  List of internal recipients 
•  List of internal Cc recipients 
•  Original Body (either in plain text or HTML format) 
•  Original Question 
•  Choices, as individual hyperlinks to a .NET active server page (ASP) that records the vote 
•  Payload, which is the contents of the Variables grid from the Inbox 

Text in the Subject, Category, Body, Question, and Choices, as well as payload captions, can be 
translated and formatted based on the default language specified for the recipient user in the Users form. 

When the recipients vote by clicking the link in the email, their Windows-default Web browser opens, or 
opens a new tab if applicable, and sends the information from the link they clicked to the ASP URL that 
was included (and hidden) in the email. This URL is built by the system based on the web server list. 

The ASP then registers the vote programmatically, as if the recipient had logged in to the system, 
displayed the same message in the Inbox, and selected the corresponding Choice button on the 
Response tab. 

The Web page then displays a success or failure message. 

The message displays both in email and in the Inbox form, but only one response is allowed: 

• 

• 

If users respond from email first, when they display the Inbox (properly refreshed), the message 
is expired and the buttons are inactive. 
If users respond from the Inbox first, then clicking a link in the external email brings up the Web 
page with a message that the message has expired and they already voted, using the previously 
selected choice. 

All prompts and notifications will go to the Inbox as well as any external email you have set 
up unless you select an Action Type Send Email.    

Troubleshooting email problems 

If you have issues with email, go to the Event Handler Status form and view the record for the event in 
question. If the email was not sent, this will be detailed in the Result section of the Handler tab.  

You will not be able to send external email from within the classroom training environment 
due to firewalls.

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  169 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Voting rules 

When a prompt is sent to a single recipient, the result of the prompt is the return value from that 
recipient's choice. However, when a prompt is sent to multiple recipients, you must select a vote counting 
method to determine the result of the prompt and include a Voting Rule parameter in your event action 
definition. 

Rule 

Majority 

Plurality 

ConditionalPlurality 

Description 

A choice must receive more than 50% of the vote to win. As 
soon as more than 50% of the recipients respond with a 
particular choice, that choice wins. 

Note: If you use the Majority rule, you should use a Voting 
Tie parameter (VOTINGTIE) to tell the system how to 
handle a tied vote. 

The choice with the highest number of votes wins, even if it 
does not receive more than 50% of the vote. 

For example, if three choices are offered, and:  

•  The first choice receives 24% of the vote; 

•  The second choice receives 43% of the vote; and 

•  The third choice receives the remaining 33% of the vote; 

then the second-choice wins, even though it received less 
than 50% of the total vote. 

Note: If you use the Plurality rule, you should use a Voting 
Tie parameter (VOTINGTIE) to tell the system how to 
handle a tied winning vote. 

The choice with the highest number of votes wins, but only if 
a specified minimum percentage of votes is reached. 

For example, if three choices are offered to 19 recipients, 
and you specify a minimum of 40% to win, then: 

•  In an 8-7-4 split, the choice with eight votes would win 

because it meets the minimum percentage. 

•  In a 7-6-6 split, there would be no winner, because no 

choice meets the minimum percentage.  

In the second case, the system must deal with the vote as 
an indeterminate result. (Had this been a simple Plurality 
vote, the choice that reaches seven votes in a 7-6-6 split 
would win.) 

Note: If you use the ConditionalPlurality rule, you must also 
include: 

•  A Minimum Percentage (MINIMUM) parameter. 

•  A Voting Tie parameter (VOTINGTIE) or Voting Disparity 
parameter (VOTINGDISPARITY) to tell the system how 
to handle the indeterminate vote. 

170   Lesson 12: Voting 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
Rule 

MinimumCount 

MinimumPercentage 

EarliestResponse 

PreferredChoice 

Description 

The first choice to reach a specified minimum number of 
votes wins. 

For example, if three choices are offered to 13 recipients, 
and you specify a minimum of five votes to win, the first 
choice to receive five votes automatically wins. 

As soon as the minimum count is reached, event execution 
moves immediately to the next action. In this case, the 
system expires any responses not yet received, and no 
further voting can take place. 

Note: If you use the MinimumCount rule, you must also 
include a Minimum Count (MINIMUM) parameter. 

The first choice to receive a specified percentage of the vote 
wins. The percentage is based on the number of recipients 
of the prompt, not the number of respondents. 

As soon as the minimum percentage is reached for a 
choice, event execution moves immediately to the next 
action. In this case, the system expires any responses not 
yet received, and no further voting can take place. 

Note: If you use this rule, you must also include a Minimum 
Percentage (MINIMUM) parameter. 

The first response to the prompt wins, regardless of the 
choice. 

As soon as the first response is received, event execution 
moves immediately to the next action. In this case, the 
system expires any responses not yet received, and no 
further voting can take place. 

If any one respondent votes for the preferred choice, that 
choice wins. In a case where none of the respondents 
select the preferred choice, then this rule behaves like the 
Plurality rule for the remaining choices. 

For example, if you have three choices, and you specify the 
first choice as the preferred choice, then: 

•  If anyone votes for the first choice, that choice wins. 

•  If the end vote is a 0-6-5 split, the second-choice wins. 

As soon as the preferred choice receives a vote, event 
execution moves immediately to the next action. In this 
case, the system expires any responses not yet received, 
and no further voting can take place. 

Note: If you use this rule, you must also include a Preferred 
Choice (PREFCHOICE) parameter to specify which choice 
is the preferred choice. 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  171 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Rule 

Description 

MinimumCount PreferredChoice 

MinimumPercentagePreferredChoice 

If a specified number of votes for a specified choice is cast, 
that choice wins.  

For example, if you set the Minimum to 3 for a Preferred 
Choice of "Approve," and three recipients respond with 
"Approve," the preferred choice wins. If less than that 
number of votes are cast for that choice after all recipients 
have responded, the vote reverts to Plurality. (In that case, 
the preferred choice may still win.) Note that when you set 
the Minimum to 1, this rule behaves exactly like Preferred 
Choice. 

Note: If you use this rule, you must also include a Minimum 
(MINIMUM) parameter to specify the minimum count, and a 
Preferred Choice (PREFCHOICE) parameter to specify 
which choice is the preferred choice. 

If a specified percentage of votes for a specified choice is 
cast, that choice wins.  

For example, if you set the Minimum to 25% for a Preferred 
Choice of "Approve," and two of eight of recipients respond 
with "Approve," the preferred choice wins. If less than that 
percentage of votes are cast for that choice after all 
recipients have responded, the vote reverts to Plurality. (In 
that case, the preferred choice may still win.) 

Note: If you use this rule, you must also include a Minimum 
(MINIMUM) parameter to specify the minimum percentage, 
and a Preferred Choice (PREFCHOICE) parameter to 
specify which choice is the preferred choice. 

172   Lesson 12: Voting 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
Dealing with indeterminate voting results 

The following situations create "indeterminate" voting results and set action attributes that are exposed as 
event functions that can be evaluated by subsequent event actions: 

•  Any disagreement among multiple recipients, registered as soon as a disagreement is detected 
o  The associated event function is the VOTINGDISPARITY( ), which is a Boolean function that 

indicates only that there was a disagreement. 

•  A tie in the case of a Plurality or Majority vote, registered at the point when all responses have 

been received or when the timeout period has expired 
o  The associated event function is the VOTINGTIE( ), which is a Boolean function that 

indicates only that there was a tie. 

You can use the returns from these functions, along with the functions RECIPIENTS(), RESPONDERS(), 
RECIPIENTLIST(), RESPONDERLIST(), and NONRESPONDERLIST() to take further actions, such as: 

•  Reprompting all the recipients and try to get a consensus. 
•  Reprompting only a select group of the respondents and urging them to adopt a different choice. 
•  Reprompting only recipients who have not yet responded. 
•  Taking some other predetermined action. 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

_________________________________________________________________________ 

v10 Using the Application Event System Training Workbook (10.18)  173 

© 2018 Infor Education. All rights reserved. No part of this Training Workbook may be reproduced or transmitted in any form, without written permission. 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Quorums 

On a Prompt action type, a quorum is automatically calculated based on: 

•  The number of recipients,  
•  The voting rule, and  
•  Any voting parameters set, such as Minimum.  

If there are several votes by whose tally a voting result can be determined unambiguously, that number is 
the quorum. Otherwise, the quorum is the number of recipients, that is, everyone has a chance to vote 
unless a timeout expires. As soon as the quorum is reached, voting is closed, any remaining unvoted 
messages are expired, and the event continues to the subsequent event action. 

However, if you specify a Quorum value, that overrides the automatic calculation. For example, if a 
message requiring a response is sent to 10 people, but you want a quorum to be reached when only four 
have voted, then specify 4 as the Quorum value. 

By default, if Quorum is not specified or is specified with a positive value, Wait for Quorum is True; that is, 
the event waits until the quorum is reached before it continues with the next event action. If Quorum is 
specified with a non-positive value, the Wait for Quorum default value is False. If these settings conflict, 
for example Quorum = 3 and Wait for Quorum is False, the system displays an error message. 

If Wait for Quorum is False, the event does not wait for a quorum to be reached. As soon as the 
messages are sent, execution continues with the next event action. If the system is not waiting for a 
quorum, the event designer needs to determine when a quorum is reached and what further actions to 
take. This can be done using VOTINGRESULT(), RESPONDERS(), RECIPIENTS(), etc., in combination 
with the Wait or Sleep actions. 

174   Lesson 12: Voting

votes wins.

regardless of the choice.

Event action types 

This table lists and describes the action types available for use when defining event actions.  

Note: Adjourning event action types (that is, Prompt, Wait, and Sleep) cannot be assigned to event 
actions on a transactional event handler.  

Mid-tier event action types (that is, Call IDO Method, Dispatch IDO Request, Execute IDO Request, Load 
Collection, Load IDO Row, and Update Collection) cannot be executed on a synchronous event handler 
whose event is fired from the database layer (that is, via FireEventSp, or attached to any Session 
framework event). If this is attempted, the handler fails with an error.

Dispatch 
IDO 
Request 

This action type dispatches an IDO request 
to execute some action on a system to 
which the user is not currently connected 
or signed in. 

This IDO request can be, for example, to 
load a collection, update a collection, or 
invoke an IDO method on an IDO runtime 
service at another "enterprise" (for 
example, one of your customers or 
vendors who also uses the same 
Mongoose application) or with another site 
in your own enterprise. 

This action type opens a session on the 
remote database server, performs the 
requested action, and closes the session. If 
appropriate, this action type also receives 
any response data from the remote 
database server and places it in a return 
variable or return parameter. You can then 
use the Transform XML action type to 
parse the return data. 

Execute IDO 
Request 

This action type executes an IDO request 
on the system to which the user is currently 
connected or signed in. 

•  IDO Request 

No 

XML 

•  Response 

This IDO request can be, for example, to 
load a collection, update a collection, or 
invoke an IDO method. 

This action type: 

Optionally, opens a new session (closing it 
when the requested action is finished). 

Performs the requested action. If 
appropriate, receives any response data 
generated by the IDO action and places it 
in a return variable or return parameter. 
You can then use the Transform XML 
action type to parse the return data. 

Ends the handler execution with an error 
status when a specified condition is met 
and, optionally, specifies a failure or error

Action type  What it does 

Notify 

This action type sends a system-generated 
message to recipients (system users), 
optionally when a specified condition is 
met. 

This notification is transmitted internally 
within the WinStudio system, without 
having to use external email or other 
messaging systems. 

Associated event

Prompt 

This action type sends a system-generated 
message to recipients (system users) and 
awaits a response from each. 

It also sends an e-mail to recipients for 
whom Send E-mail Prompts is specified in 
the Users form. To send emails for 
prompts, you must have an SMTP server 
designated on the Intranets form and 
automatic relaying of email messages 
configured on the SMTP server. 

This action type counts votes according to 
a specified rule. If no response or an 
insufficient response is received within a 
certain period, it optionally goes to an 
alternate action, such as these: 

Perform an alternate prompt to an alternate 
set of recipients 

Set a default and branch to the subsequent 
event action 

Go directly to the subsequent event action 
(the same as if a sufficient number of 
responses were received)

Action type  What it does 

Sleep 

Waits until a specified period of time has 
elapsed before proceeding to the next 
action 

Transform 
XML 

This action type takes XML as input and 
transforms it for use elsewhere. 

This action type transforms specified XML, 
based on transformation rules contained in 
the XSLT, with the resulting XML stored in 
a result variable or parameter. 

A transform XML operation can range from 
simple (picking out a single specific 
element from a large document, to be used 
as part of a SUBSTITUTE expression in a 
Notify action) to complex (translating an 
entire document from one format to 
another, to be used as input to some other 
process). 

This action type updates an IDO collection 
by inserting, updating, or deleting records 
within that collection. 

Using this action type, you can either 
update a collection directly from a specified 
IDO, or you can update a collection that is 
already loaded into a named result set. 

This action type instructs the system to 
wait for a specified condition to be met 
before proceeding to the next action. 

If the condition does not become true 
within a certain time, optionally goes to an 
alternate action. 

A retest interval of zero (0) means that the 
condition is never retested. 

A timeout setting of zero (0) means that the 
event action never times out, that is, that it 
waits indefinitely.

Collection 

Wait

Event action parameters 

The Event Action Parameters table lists (in alphabetic order) and describes all the event action 
parameters and their functions.  

When using the Event Action Parameters table, keep these points in mind: 

This… 

ALLCAPS 

Parentheses () 

Equal signs (=) 

Commas 

Content in italics 

Refers to this… 

Functions and punctuation to be specified and stored verbatim 

Content that varies according to the context, for example, for a 
SUBJECT(expr) parameter, expr represents the actual content that is 
sent in the message 

Ellipses (…) 

Indicates more like the preceding element, separated by commas 

Parentheses indicate that the repetition of elements is optional. 

scalarExpr 

Scalar (numeric, string, date, or typeless) event expressions 

Boolean 

name 

var (variable) parm 
(parameter) collection 

A Boolean event expression 

Identifiers used for named or contextual purposes 

These identifiers can consist of: 

•  An initial uppercase or lowercase letter or underscore ( _ ), followed 

by  

•  Any combination of letters, numerals, underscores, square brackets ( 

[ ]), and/or periods. 

Prop (property) 

This specifies the property name as a string expression. 

To specify the property name as a literal value, enclose it in double 
quotation marks (" "). 

action 

Event action sequence number (values to be adjusted automatically if 
actions are resequenced) 

The following is the Event Actions Parameters table:

can be used to build an expression

This parameter indicates a list of 
secondary recipients of the message, 
delimited by semi-colons (;). Do not 
leave spaces between multiple 
recipients in the list. 

For Notify and Prompt actions, 
recipients are identified by their user 
IDs on the system. For Send Email 
actions, recipients are identified by 
their email addresses. 

This parameter indicates a comma-
separated list of return values and 
button labels (or link labels for e 
mail). Note that the parser strips out 
whitespace, so it is OK to include 
spaces between items in the list. 

In each pair, the first item is the value 
to be returned if the recipient selects 
that option. The second item is the 
label that appears on the selection 
button/link. For the button/link labels, 
you can use strings defined in the 
Strings table or literal values. For 
emails, strings are translated and 
formatted based on the Default 
Language specified for the recipient

("").

This parameter changes method 
parameter values during an 
IdoOnInvoke event. paramNumber is 
the 1- based position of the 
parameter to change. scalarExpr is 
the value to which the parameter is to 
be set. For multiple parameters, 
include them as a comma-separated 
list. 

Count indicates the minimum number 
of votes required for a choice to win. 
It must be used in conjunction with a 
ConditionalPlurality, or 
MinimumCount voting rule. 

Percentage indicates the minimum 
percentage of the total vote (based 
on recipients of the message) 
required for a choice to win. It must 
be used in conjunction with a 
MinimumPercentage voting rule. 

This parameter specifies how 
message payload elements that 
represent modified properties are 
handled: 

Default – The modified parts of the 
payload are visible; the recipient can 
further modify any of their contents. 

Hidden – The modified parts of the 
payload are hidden, for example, for 
a secret ballot. 

Read-Only – The modified parts of 
the payload are display only, so the 
recipient cannot further modify the 
contents. 

This specification applies to event 
message variables with names in the 
form Row.Property that have a 
corresponding

n 

•  Load 
IDO 
Row 

This parameter specifies the name of 
a valid property to be used for the 
sort order on the collection when it is 
loaded and displayed. For example, if 
you select CreateDate as the 
property for this field, the system 
sorts the collection according to the 
dates on which transactions were 
recorded. 

You can use multiple properties, and 
the system prioritizes multiple 
properties in the order in which they 
are listed. In other words, the first 
property would be the primary 
property for sorting; the next property 
would be the secondary property for 
sorting; and so on. Multiple 
properties must be specified as a 
comma-separated list. 

OPTIMISTICLOCKING( 

Boolean) 

ORDERBY(scalarExpr) 

ORDERBY("PoLine") 

ORDERBY("CoRelease 
ASC, CoItem") 

Note that, in the second 
example, there is an 
attribute "ASC" specified. 
This tells the system to 
sort the list in ascending 
order, which is also the 
default. You could instead 
use DESC to tell the 
system to sort the list in 
descending order.

e 
Method 

This parameter specifies a comma-
separated list of parameters required 
by the IDO method or stored 
procedure. 

If an event variable is named using 
this function and that variable does 

SET(RV(var)  | RE(param) 
= 

scalarExpr [, ... ] ) 

Each RV or RE 
represents a name-name 
pair. var is the name of an 
event variable; param is 
the name of an event 
parameter; scalarExpr 
evaluates to a property 
name of the IDO that was 
loaded. 

Example: 

SET(RV(myVar) = "")

= 

scalarExpr [, ... ]) 

Each RV or RE 
represents a name-name 
pair. In the case of a 
Generate Event action, 
the scalarExpr evaluates 
to the name of an event 
output parameter of the 
generated event. In the 
case of a Call Web 
Service action, the 
scalarExpr evaluates to 
the name of a node in the 
response XML. 

Example:

"rows_succeeded", 
RE(PostResult) = 
"result_message" )

This parameter is used only for the 
SessionOnVarChanged framework 
event. It specifies a value to be 
assigned to the session variable that, 
when changed, generated the event. 
This value replaces whatever value 
was requested by the process that 
initiated the change. In effect, this 
overrides the original change request 
behind the scenes. 

For example, suppose you have an 
event that is set to be executed 
whenever a user tries to reset a 
session variable. This event can be 
used to override the user-initiated 
change and reset the variable to 
whatever value you designate here.

comma-separated list.

event is executed, the system 
creates the variable when needed. 

TIP: Including a null value for a 
variable (such as myVar = ) 
generates a syntax error. To 
designate a null value for the value of 
a variable, use a double set of 
quotation marks (myVar = "").

quotes
